## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / kinetic ODE modeling)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is explicitly the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the standard setup for chemical kinetics via ordinary differential equations. With only (t, A) available, the most likely relationships are classical kinetic rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, reversibility, autocatalysis) and possibly explicitly on t (time-varying rate constants, catalyst deactivation, external forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption/production: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate regime; e.g., surface-limited or constant feed)
- First-order decay (unimolecular / pseudo-first-order): dA_dt = -c0 * A (exponential decay of A)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular self-reaction or effective second-order kinetics)
- nth-order power-law rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (general empirical reaction order c1)
- Offset power-law (background/impurity concentration): dA_dt = -c0 * (A + c1)**c2 (accounts for baseline shift in measured A)
- Approach to equilibrium (linear relaxation): dA_dt = c0 * (c1 - A) (reversible first-order kinetics toward equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth then saturation due to limiting reagent)
- Reversible mass-action with forward/backward-like terms: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 (net of a first-order loss and constant source/back reaction lumped)
- Time-varying first-order rate constant (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (rate constant changes over time, e.g., temperature ramp approximated vs t)
- Catalyst deactivation / aging factor: dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective activity decays with time, slowing the reaction)
- Induction or activation period: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) * A (rate ramps up from 0 to steady kinetics)
- Periodic forcing (light chopping, mixing cycles): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (periodically modulated first-order kinetics)
- Mixed-order (parallel pathways): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular and bimolecular contributions)
- Empirical polynomial-in-time rate coefficient: dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t + c2 * t**2) * A (smooth time dependence of effective first-order kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is proportional to A, the process is effectively first-order (straight line in ln(A) vs t for solutions), implying a single-species loss mechanism.
- If dA_dt scales like A**2 (or higher powers), early-time decay is much faster at high A and slows dramatically as A decreases, consistent with bimolecular or higher-order steps.
- A term of the form (c1 - A) indicates relaxation toward a steady-state/equilibrium concentration c1 (sign of dA_dt flips around A = c1).
- An A*(c1 - A) structure suggests autocatalysis with depletion/limitation, producing an S-shaped A(t) while keeping A bounded by c1.
- Explicit time dependence in an effective rate coefficient, e.g., (c0 + c1*t), points to externally changing conditions (ramp experiments) or gradual drift in system properties.
- Multiplying the kinetics by exp(-c*t) indicates progressive loss of reactivity (catalyst deactivation, fouling, light attenuation, or inhibitor buildup modeled implicitly by time).
- A prefactor (1 - exp(-c*t)) captures induction/activation: initially slow reaction that accelerates as some intermediate/catalyst becomes available.
- A constant additive term in dA_dt (e.g., +c1) often represents a feed/source term or a lumped back-reaction that does not depend on A over the observed range.
- Sinusoidal dependence on t suggests periodic forcing (pulsed irradiation, oscillatory mixing, cyclic temperature control), causing oscillations in dA_dt even at fixed A.

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK13)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A + c1*_p*sin(c2*A)
Candidate formulas: 70

GT is a fixed function of **A only** (no dependence on *t*):
\[
f(A)= -0.23236613283613416\,A + 0.395876449251558\,\sin(0.5265654762365851\,A).
\]
So any matching candidate must be reducible (by choosing its free constants) to **(linear in A) + (constant amplitude)·sin(constant·A + phase)**, with **no other A-nonlinear terms** and **no t-dependence**.

---

### 1. \(A^3 c0\sin(c1 t+c2)+A c3+c4\sin(A c5+c6)\)
Set \(c0=0\) to remove the \(t\)-dependent term. Then it’s \(A c3 + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)\), which can match GT by choosing \(c3=-0.232366...\), \(c4=0.395876...\), \(c5=0.526565...\), \(c6=0\). **Matches.**

### 2. \(A c0 + A c1/(c2+t)^3 + c3(A+c4)^3 + c5(c6+t)^{c7}\sin(Ac8+c9)\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence: set \(c1=0\) and either \(c5=0\) or force \((c6+t)^{c7}\) constant (not possible for all \(t\) unless \(c7=0\), but then still constant factor OK). Also must remove cubic term: set \(c3=0\). Then reduces to \(A c0 + c5\sin(Ac8+c9)\) (if \(c7=0\)). Choose \(c0, c5, c8, c9\) to match GT (with \(c9=0\)). **Matches.**

### 3. \(\frac{A^3 c0}{A^2 c1+1}+\frac{A^2 c2\sin(Ac3+c4)}{A^2 c1+1}+\frac{A c5}{A^2 c1+1}+\frac{A c6}{A^2 c1+1}\)
To avoid rational-in-\(A\) distortion, set \(c1=0\) so denominator is 1. Then expression is \(A^3 c0 + A^2 c2\sin(\cdot)+A(c5+c6)\). Must kill \(A^3\) and \(A^2\sin\) terms: set \(c0=0, c2=0\). Left with \(A(c5+c6)\) only, cannot produce sine term. **No match.**

### 4. \(A c0 + c1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\)
GT has no constant offset, so set \(c1=0\). Then choose \(c0=-0.232366...\), \(c2=0.395876...\), \(c3=0.526565...\), \(c4=0\). **Matches.**

### 5. \(A^2 c0 + A c1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\)
Must remove \(A^2\) term: set \(c0=0\). Then it’s \(A c1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\) and match as in #4 with \(c1=-0.232366...\), etc. **Matches.**

### 6. \(A c0 + c1(A+c2)^{c3} + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)\)
Need to eliminate the power term for all \(A\): easiest set \(c1=0\). Then match linear+sine with \(c0=-0.232366...\), \(c4=0.395876...\), \(c5=0.526565...\), \(c6=0\). **Matches.**

### 7. \(A c0 + A c1 + c2 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\)
Combine linear terms: \(A(c0+c1)\). Set \(c2=0\). Choose \(c0+c1=-0.232366...\), \(c3=0.395876...\), \(c4=0.526565...\), \(c5=0\). **Matches.**

### 8. \(A c0 + A c1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\)
Same idea: set \(c0+c1=-0.232366...\), \(c2=0.395876...\), \(c3=0.526565...\), \(c4=0\). **Matches.**

### 9. \(A c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)\)
Directly the GT form (no constant offset). Choose \(c0=-0.232366...\), \(c1=0.395876...\), \(c2=0.526565...\), \(c3=0\). **Matches.**

### 10. \(\frac{A^3 c0}{A^2 c1+1}+\frac{A c2}{A^2 c1+1}+c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\)
To avoid rational term, set \(c1=0\) so first two become \(A^3 c0 + A c2\). Must set \(c0=0\). Then \(A c2 + c3\sin(\cdot)\) matches GT by parameter choice. **Matches.**

### 11. \(A c0 + A^{c1} c2 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\)
Must remove \(A^{c1}\) term: set \(c2=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 12. \(A c0 + A^{c1} c2 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\cos(c6 t)\)
GT has no \(t\). Need \(\cos(c6 t)\) constant for all \(t\): set \(c6=0\) so \(\cos(0)=1\). Also remove \(A^{c1}c2\) via \(c2=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 13. \(A c0 + \frac{A c1}{A^2 c2+1} + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\)
To make the rational linear term purely linear, set \(c2=0\) so it becomes \(A c1\). Then total linear is \(A(c0+c1)\). Match with \(c0+c1=-0.232366...\), sine params as GT. **Matches.**

### 14. \(A^3 c0 + A c1 + A c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\)
Sine term is multiplied by \(A\); GT sine amplitude is constant. Only way to remove that is \(c2=0\), but then no sine. So cannot match. **No match.**

### 15. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(Ac2+c3) + c4 e^{c5 t}\sin(Ac6+c7)\)
Has \(A\sin(\cdot)\) term (wrong amplitude dependence) unless \(c1=0\). Then remaining sine term has \(t\)-dependent amplitude unless set \(c4=0\) (kills sine) or \(c5=0\) (constant amplitude). If \(c1=0\) and \(c5=0\), we get \(A c0 + c4\sin(Ac6+c7)\) which matches GT. **Matches.**

### 16. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(Ac2+c3) + A^{c4} c5\)
Again \(A\sin\) wrong unless \(c1=0\). Then need \(A^{c4}c5\) to be constant-amplitude sine? impossible; must set \(c5=0\). Leaves only linear term, no sine. **No match.**

### 17. \(\frac{A^3 c0}{A^2 c1+1} + A^3 c2 + A c3\)
No sine term at all. **No match.**

### 18. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(Ac2+c3) + c4 e^{A c5}\)
Need constant-amplitude sine: must set \(c1=0\) (otherwise \(A\sin\)). Then exponential term must become sine—impossible; set \(c4=0\) removes it, leaving only linear. **No match.**

### 19. \(A c0 + A c1/(c2+t)^3 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5) + c6(A+c7)^3\)
Remove \(t\)-term: \(c1=0\). Remove cubic: \(c6=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 20. Rational expression with \((A^{c0}+c2)\) denominator plus sine terms
To match GT (no denominator), would need denominator constant: set \(c0=0\) so \(A^{0}=1\), denominator \(1+c2\) constant. Then expression becomes a linear combination of \(A\), constant, and \(\sin(Ac6+c7)\) all scaled by constant \(1/(1+c2)\). Set constant offset to 0 by choosing numerator constant term 0 (via \(c4=0\) and/or \(c8=0\) and \(c2\) choices). Then choose remaining parameters to match linear and sine coefficients. **Matches.**

### 21. Like #3 plus extra sine-over-denominator
Set \(c1=0\) to remove denominator. Then terms include \(A^3 c0\) and \(A^2 c2\sin(\cdot)\) which must be zero: set \(c0=0, c2=0\). Remaining is \(A(c5+c6)+ c7\sin(Ac3+c8)\), which matches GT. **Matches.**

### 22. \(A c0 e^{c1 t} + A c2 + c3 e^{c4 t} + c5 e^{c6 t}\sin(Ac7+c8)\)
Need no \(t\): set \(c1=0, c4=0, c6=0\). Also GT has no constant term: set \(c3=0\). Then linear term is \(A(c0+c2)\) and sine term constant amplitude. Match parameters. **Matches.**

### 23. Denominator \(A^5+c1\) etc.
To avoid nontrivial rational dependence, would need denominator constant, impossible since it contains \(A^5\). No way to cancel for all \(A\) while keeping sine+linear. **No match.**

### 24. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(Ac2+c3) + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)\)
Must remove \(A\sin\) term: set \(c1=0\). Then \(A c0 + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)\) matches GT. **Matches.**

### 25. \(A c0 + c1(A+c2)^2 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5) + c6 e^{A c7}\)
Need remove quadratic and exponential: set \(c1=0, c6=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 26. \(A c0 + c1\log(A^3 c2+1) + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\)
Remove log term: set \(c1=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 27. Like #3 but with \(A^2\sin\) and also \(\sin\) over denominator
Set \(c1=0\). Then must kill \(A^3 c0\) and \(A^2 c2\sin\): set \(c0=0, c2=0\). Left with \(A c5 + c6\sin(Ac3+c4)\), matches GT. **Matches.**

### 28. \(A^2 c0 e^{c1 t} + A c2 e^{c3 t} + A c4 + c5\sin(Ac6+c7)\)
Need no \(t\): set \(c1=0, c3=0\). Then there is an \(A^2 c0\) term; set \(c0=0\). Linear term \(A(c2+c4)\) plus sine matches GT. **Matches.**

### 29. \(A c0 + \frac{c1}{c2 + A^{-3}} + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\)
The middle term is a non-polynomial rational function of \(A\) (equals \(c1 A^3/(c2 A^3+1)\)). To match GT (which has only linear+sine), must set \(c1=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 30. \(A c0 + \frac{A^{c1} c2}{A^{c1}+c3} + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)\)
The fraction term is generally nonlinear in \(A\); to remove it set \(c2=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 31. \(A c0 + A c1/(c2+t)^3 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\)
Remove \(t\)-term by \(c1=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 32. \(A c0 + A^{c1} c2\log(c3 t+1) + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c2=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 33. \(A^2 c0 + A c1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4) + c5\sin(Ac6+c7)\cos(c8 t)\)
Need no \(t\): set \(c5=0\) (or \(c8=0\) but then extra sine remains). Also remove \(A^2\): set \(c0=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 34. Rational terms plus \(\sin(c4 e^{A c5}+c6)\)
Even if set \(c1=0\) and \(c0=0\) to simplify rational part to linear, the sine argument is \(c4 e^{A c5}+c6\), not linear in \(A\). Only way out is set \(c3=0\) (kills sine), then cannot match GT. **No match.**

### 35. Rational terms plus \(c3 e^{c4 t}\sin(Ac5+c6)\)
Set \(c1=0\) and \(c0=0\) to remove \(A^3\). Then rational linear becomes \(A c2\). Remove \(t\)-dependence by setting \(c4=0\) so \(e^{0}=1\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 36. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + A c4/(c5 t+c6) + c7/(c5 t+c6)\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, must set \(c4=0, c7=0\) (or make denominator constant impossible for all \(t\) unless \(c5=0\), but then still constants remain; easiest zero them). Still have \(A\sin\) term; must set \(c1=0\), leaving only linear. **No match.**

### 37. \(A c0 + c1(A+c2)^2 + c3 e^{A c4} + c5 e^{c6 t}\sin(Ac7+c8)\)
Remove quadratic and exponential-in-A: set \(c1=0, c3=0\). Remove \(t\)-dependence by \(c6=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 38. \(A c0 e^{c1 t} + A c2 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5) + c6 e^{c7 t}\)
Set \(c1=0\) and \(c7=0\) to remove \(t\). Then constant term \(c6\) must be 0. Match linear+sine with \(A(c0+c2)\). **Matches.**

### 39. \(A c0 e^{c1 t} + A c2 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)\)
Set \(c1=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 40. \(A c0 + c1 e^{c2 t} + c3\sin(Ac4+c5) + c6 e^{c7 t}\)
Remove \(t\)-terms: set \(c1=0, c6=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 41. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4\log(c5 e^{A c6 + c7 t}+1)\)
Has \(A\sin\) term (must set \(c1=0\)). Log term depends on \(A\) (and possibly \(t\)); to remove it set \(c4=0\). Then only linear remains. **No match.**

### 42. \(A^2 c0 + A c1 + A c2 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5) + c6\)
Set \(c0=0\) and \(c6=0\). Linear term \(A(c1+c2)\) plus sine matches GT. **Matches.**

### 43. \(A^2 c0 + A c1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4) + c5\)
Set \(c0=0, c5=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 44. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4 t/(c5 t+c6) + c7/(c5 t+c6)\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c4=0, c7=0\). Then still \(A\sin\) term; set \(c1=0\). Leaves only linear. **No match.**

### 45. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4\sin(c5\log(c6 e^{A c7}+1)+c8)\)
Need constant-amplitude sine with linear argument; last term is highly nonlinear in \(A\). If set \(c4=0\), lose sine; if keep it, can’t make it \(\sin(kA)\) for all \(A\). Also \(A\sin\) term forces \(c1=0\). **No match.**

### 46. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + A c4 e^{c5/(c6+t)}\)
To remove \(t\)-dependence in exponential factor, would need \(c5=0\) so factor is 1, giving extra linear term \(A c4\). But still \(A\sin\) term must be removed (\(c1=0\)), leaving only linear. **No match.**

### 47. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4 e^{c5 t}|A|^{c6}\)
Remove \(t\) by \(c4=0\) (or \(c5=0\) but still \(|A|^{c6}\) nonlinearity). Also must remove \(A\sin\) via \(c1=0\). Leaves only linear. **No match.**

### 48. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + A c4 e^{c5 t}\)
Remove \(t\) by \(c5=0\) giving extra linear \(A c4\). Still must remove \(A\sin\) via \(c1=0\). Leaves only linear. **No match.**

### 49. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4 e^{c5 t}\)
Remove \(t\) by setting \(c4=0\) (or \(c5=0\) then constant offset remains, but can set \(c4=0\) anyway). Then must set \(c1=0\) to remove \(A\sin\), leaving only linear. **No match.**

### 50. \(A c0 + c1 e^{c2 t} + c3 e^{c4 t} + c5\sin(Ac6+c7)\cos(c8 t)\)
Need no \(t\): set \(c1=0, c3=0\) and set \(c8=0\) so \(\cos(0)=1\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 51. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + A c4 e^{c5 t} + A c6\)
Remove \(t\) by \(c5=0\) giving linear \(A c4\). Still \(A\sin\) must be removed: \(c1=0\). Then only linear remains. **No match.**

### 52. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4 e^{c5\sin(Ac6+c7 t+c8)}\)
Nonlinear exponential-of-sine term; to remove set \(c4=0\). Then must set \(c1=0\) (remove \(A\sin\)). Only linear remains. **No match.**

### 53. \(A c0 + c1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)\cos(c5 t)\)
Remove \(t\) by \(c5=0\) so cosine is 1. Remove constant offset by \(c1=0\). Then match linear+sine. **Matches.**

### 54. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + A c4/(A c5+c6) + c7/(A c5+c6)\)
These rational-in-\(A\) terms cannot combine to yield purely linear+sine for all \(A\) unless set \(c4=0, c7=0\). Then must set \(c1=0\) (remove \(A\sin\)). Only linear remains. **No match.**

### 55. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + A^{c4}c5/(A^{c4}+c6)\)
The fraction term is nonlinear in \(A\) unless removed by \(c5=0\). Then must set \(c1=0\). Only linear remains. **No match.**

### 56. \(A c0 + c1(A+c2)^2 + c3 e^{A c4} + c5\sin(c6 e^{A c7}+c8)\)
To get GT form, must remove quadratic and exponentials and nonlinear sine argument: set \(c1=0, c3=0, c5=0\). Then only linear remains. **No match.**

### 57. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4 t + c5\)
Remove \(t\) by \(c4=0\). Remove constant by \(c5=0\). Still \(A\sin\) forces \(c1=0\). Only linear remains. **No match.**

### 58. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4 t/(A c5+c6) + c7/(A c5+c6)\)
Has explicit \(t\) unless \(c4=0\). Then rational term remains unless \(c7=0\). Still \(A\sin\) forces \(c1=0\). Only linear remains. **No match.**

### 59. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + A c4\sin(c5 t+c6)\)
To remove \(t\), set \(c4=0\). Then \(A\sin\) forces \(c1=0\). Only linear remains. **No match.**

### 60. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + A c4\sin(c5 t+c6) + A c7\)
Remove \(t\) by \(c4=0\). Then \(A\sin\) forces \(c1=0\). Only linear remains. **No match.**

### 61. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4\log(c5|A|+1)\cos(c6 t+c7)\)
Remove \(t\) by making cosine constant: set \(c6=0\) so \(\cos(c7)\) constant, but log(|A|) term still non-GT unless \(c4=0\). Then \(A\sin\) forces \(c1=0\). Only linear remains. **No match.**

### 62. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)\sin(c7 t+c8)\)
To remove \(t\), set \(c4=0\) (or \(c7=0\) gives constant \(\sin(c8)\) factor, but still extra sine-in-A term could be okay; however still have \(A\sin\) term). Need \(A\sin\) removed: \(c1=0\). If \(c4\neq 0\) and \(c7=0\), we could keep constant-amplitude sine term; then expression becomes \(A c0 + (c4\sin(c8))\sin(Ac5+c6)\), which matches GT. **Matches** (take \(c1=0, c7=0\), and tune \(c4\sin(c8)\)).

### 63. \(A c0 + A^{c1}c2/(A^{c1}+c3) + c4 e^{c5\sin(Ac6+c7)}\)
Exponential-of-sine term cannot become linear+sine unless removed: set \(c4=0\). Fraction term must be removed too: set \(c2=0\). Leaves only linear, no sine. **No match.**

### 64. \(A^2 c0 + A c1 + A c2\sin(\cdot) + A c5\)
Sine term multiplied by \(A\); must set \(c2=0\) losing sine. Even if \(c0=0\), left only linear. **No match.**

### 65. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4\log(Ac5+1)\)
Need constant-amplitude sine, so set \(c1=0\). Log term must be removed \(c4=0\). Only linear remains. **No match.**

### 66. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4\sin(c5+c6 t)\)
Remove \(t\) by \(c4=0\). Then \(A\sin\) forces \(c1=0\). Only linear remains. **No match.**

### 67. \(A c0 + A c1\sin(\cdot) + c4\log(c5|c6\sin(Ac7+c8 t+c9)|+1)\)
Nonlinear log term; remove by \(c4=0\). Then \(A\sin\) forces \(c1=0\). Only linear remains. **No match.**

### 68. \(A c0 + A c1/(c2+t)^3 + c3(A+c4)^3 + c5\log(c6 e^{A c7+c8 t}+1)\)
To remove \(t\): set \(c1=0\) and \(c5=0\). Remove cubic: \(c3=0\). Leaves only linear, no sine. **No match.**

### 69. \(A c0 + c1/(c2 + A^{-3}) + c3 e^{c4 t}|A|^{c5}\)
Remove \(t\) by setting \(c3=0\). Then remaining has \(c1/(c2+A^{-3})\) nonlinear unless \(c1=0\). Leaves only linear. **No match.**

### 70. \(A c0 + A^{c1}c2 e^{c3 t} + c4/(c5 + A^{-3})\)
Remove \(t\) by \(c2=0\) or \(c3=0\) (but term still nonlinear in \(A\)). Also last term nonlinear unless \(c4=0\). After removing nonlinear terms, only linear remains, no sine. **No match.**

Many candidates can be reduced to \(A\cdot(\text{const}) + (\text{const})\sin(\text{const}\cdot A + \text{const})\) with no \(t\)-dependence (e.g., #4, #9, etc.), hence equivalence is achievable.
